GrpcMuxImpl::processDiscoveryResources(const std::vector<DecodedResourcePtr>& resources,\n   414→                                            ApiState& api_state, const std::string& type_url,\n   415→                                            const std::string& version_info,\n   416→                                            const bool call_delegate) {\n   417→  ASSERT_IS_MAIN_OR_TEST_THREAD();\n   418→  // To avoid O(n^2) explosion (e.g. when we have 1000s of EDS watches), we\n   419→  // build a map here from resource name to resource and then walk watches_.\n   420→  // We have to walk all watches (and need an efficient map as a result) to\n   421→  // ensure we deliver empty config updates when a resource is dropped. We make the map ordered\n   422→  // for test determinism.\n   423→  absl::btree_map<std::string, DecodedResourceRef> resource_ref_map;\n   424→  std::vector<DecodedResourceRef> all_resource_refs;\n   425→\n   426→  const auto scoped_ttl_update = api_state.ttl_.scopedTtlUpdate();\n   427→\n   428→  for (const auto& resource : resources) {\n   429→    if (resource->ttl()) {\n   430→      api_state.ttl_.add(*resource->ttl(), resource->name());\n   431→    } else {\n   432→      api_state.ttl_.clear(resource->name());\n   433→    }\n   434→\n   435→    all_resource_refs.emplace_back(*resource);\n   436→    if (XdsResourceIdentifier::hasXdsTpScheme(resource->name())) {\n   437→      // Sort the context params of an xdstp resource, so we can compare xds::core::v3::ResourceName xdstp_resource = resource_or_error.value();\n   441→      XdsResourceIdentifier::EncodeOptions options;\n   442→      options.sort_context_params_ = true;\n   443→      resource_ref_map.emplace(XdsResourceIdentifier::encodeUrn(xdstp_resource, options),\n   444→                               *resource);\n   445→    } else {\n   446→      resource_ref_map.emplace(resource->name(), *resource);\n   447→    }\n   448→  }\n   449→\n   450→  // Execute external config validators if there are any watches.\n   451→  if (!api_state.watches_.empty()) {\n   452→    config_validators_->executeValidators(type_url, resources);\n   453→  }\n   454→\n   455→  for (auto watch : api_state.watches_) {\n   456→    // onConfigUpdate should be called in all cases for single watch xDS (Cluster and\n   457→    // Listener) even if the message does not have resources so that update_empty stat\n   458→    // is properly incremented and state-of-the-world semantics are maintained.\n   459→    if (watch->resources_.empty()) {\n   460→      THROW_IF_NOT_OK(watch->callbacks_.onConfigUpdate(all_resource_refs, version_info));\n   461→      continue;\n   462→    }\n   463→    std::vector<DecodedResourceRef> found_resources;\n   464→    for (const auto& watched_resource_name : watch->resources_) {\n   465→      // Look for a singleton subscription.\n   466→      auto it = resource_ref_map.find(watched_resource_name);\n   467→      if (it != resource_ref_map.end()) {\n   468→        found_resources.emplace_back(it->second);\n   469→      } else if (isXdsTpWildcard(watched_resource_name)) {\n   470→        // See if the resources match the xdstp wildcard subscription.\n   471→ {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_014gWyTHZ9xrTim12kmXXZ49","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→#pragma once\n     2→\n     3→#include \"envoy/config/subscription.h\"\n     4→#include \"envoy/config/xds_config_tracker.h\"\n     5→#include \"envoy/event/dispatcher.h\"\n     6→#include \"envoy/grpc/status.h\"\n     7→#include \"envoy/local_info/local_info.h\"\n     8→#include \"envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.pb.h\"\n     9→\n    10→#include \"source/common/common/assert.h\"\n    11→#include \"source/common/common/logger.h\"\n    12→#include \"source/common/config/api_version.h\"\n    13→#include \"source/common/config/ttl.h\"\n    14→#include \"source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/pausable_ack_queue.h\"\n    15→#include \"source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h\"\n    16→\n    17→#include \"absl/container/node_hash_map.h\"\n    18→\n    19→namespace Envoy {\n    20→namespace Config {\n    21→\n    22→// Tracks the xDS protocol state of an individual ongoing delta xDS session, i.e. a single type_url.\n    23→// There can be multiple DeltaSubscriptionStates active. They will always all be blissfully\n    24→// unaware of each other's existence, even when their messages are being multiplexed together by\n    25→// ADS.\n    26→//\n    27→// There are two scenarios which affect how DeltaSubscriptionState manages the resources. First\n    28→// scenario is when we are subscribed to a wildcard resource, and other scenario is when we are not.\n    29→//\n    30→// Delta subscription state also divides the resources it cached into three categories: requested,\n    31→// wildcard and ambiguous.\n    32→//\n    33→// The \"requested\" category is for resources that we have explicitly asked for (either through the\n    34→// initial set of resources or through the on-demand mechanism). Resources in this category are in\n    35→// one of two states: \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\".\n    36→//\n    37→// \"Complete\" resources are resources about which the server sent us the information we need (for\n    38→// now - just resource version).\n    39→//\n    40→// The \"waiting for server\" state is either for resources that we have just requested, but we still\n    41→// didn't receive any version information from the server, or for the \"complete\" resources that,\n    42→// according to the server, are gone, but we are still interested in them - in such case we strip\n    43→// the information from the resource.\n    44→//\n    45→// The \"wildcard\" category is for resources that we are not explicitly interested in, but we are\n    46→// indirectly interested through the subscription to the wildcard resource.\n    47→//\n    48→// The \"ambiguous\" category is for resources that we stopped being interested in, but we may still\n    49→// be interested indirectly through the wildcard subscription. This situation happens because of the\n    50→// xDS protocol limitation - the server isn't able to tell us that the resource we subscribed to is\n    51→// also a part of our wildcard subscription. So when we unsubscribe from the resource, we need to\n    52→// receive a confirmation from the server whether to keep the resource (which means that it was a\n    53→// part of our wildcard subscription) or to drop it.\n    54→//\n    55→// Please refer to drawings (non-wildcard-resource-state-machine.png and\n    56→// (wildcard-resource-state-machine.png) for visual depictions of the resource state machine.\n    57→//\n    58→// In the \"no wildcard subscription\" scenario all the cached resources should be in the \"requested\"\n    59→// category. Resources are added to the category upon the explicit request and dropped when we\n    60→// explicitly unsubscribe from it. Transitions between \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\" happen\n    61→// when we receive messages from the server - if a resource in the message is in \"added resources\"\n    62→// list (thus contains version information), the resource becomes \"complete\". If the resource in the\n    63→// message is in \"removed resources\" list, it changes into the \"waiting for server\" state. If a\n    64→// server sends us a resource that we didn't request, it's going to be ignored.\n    65→//\n    66→// In the \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, \"requested\" category is the same as in \"no wildcard\n    67→// subscription\" scenario, with one exception - the unsubscribed \"complete\" resource is not removed\n    68→// from the cache, but it's moved to the \"ambiguous\" resources instead. At this point we are waiting\n    69→// for the server to tell us that this resource should be either moved to the \"wildcard\" resources,\n    70→// or dropped. Resources in \"wildcard\" category are only added there or dropped from there by the\n    71→// server. Resources from both \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories can become \"requested\"\n    72→// \"complete\" resources if we subscribe to them again.\n    73→//\n    74→// The delta subscription state transitions between the two scenarios depending on whether we are\n    75→// subscribed to wildcard resource or not. They will always all be blissfully\n// unaware of each other's existence, even when their messages are being multiplexed together by\n// ADS.\n//\n// There are two scenarios which affect how DeltaSubscriptionState manages the resources. First\n// scenario is when we are subscribed to a wildcard resource, and other scenario is when we are not.\n//\n// Delta subscription state also divides the resources it cached into three categories: requested,\n// wildcard and ambiguous.\n//\n// The \"requested\" category is for resources that we have explicitly asked for (either through the\n// initial set of resources or through the on-demand mechanism). Resources in this category are in\n// one of two states: \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\".\n//\n// \"Complete\" resources are resources about which the server sent us the information we need (for\n// now - just resource version).\n//\n// The \"waiting for server\" state is either for resources that we have just requested, but we still\n// didn't receive any version information from the server, or for the \"complete\" resources that,\n// according to the server, are gone, but we are still interested in them - in such case we strip\n// the information from the resource.\n//\n// The \"wildcard\" category is for resources that we are not explicitly interested in, but we are\n// indirectly interested through the subscription to the wildcard resource.\n//\n// The \"ambiguous\" category is for resources that we stopped being interested in, but we may still\n// be interested indirectly through the wildcard subscription. This situation happens because of the\n// xDS protocol limitation - the server isn't able to tell us that the resource we subscribed to is\n// also a part of our wildcard subscription. So when we unsubscribe from the resource, we need to\n// receive a confirmation from the server whether to keep the resource (which means that it was a\n// part of our wildcard subscription) or to drop it.\n//\n// Please refer to drawings (non-wildcard-resource-state-machine.png and\n// (wildcard-resource-state-machine.png) for visual depictions of the resource state machine.\n//\n// In the \"no wildcard subscription\" scenario all the cached resources should be in the \"requested\"\n// category. Resources are added to the category upon the explicit request and dropped when we\n// explicitly unsubscribe from it. Transitions between \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\" happen\n// when we receive messages from the server - if a resource in the message is in \"added resources\"\n// list (thus contains version information), the resource becomes \"complete\". If the resource in the\n// message is in \"removed resources\" list, it changes into the \"waiting for server\" state. If a\n// server sends us a resource that we didn't request, it's going to be ignored.\n//\n// In the \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, \"requested\" category is the same as in \"no wildcard\n// subscription\" scenario, with one exception - the unsubscribed \"complete\" resource is not removed\n// from the cache, but it's moved to the \"ambiguous\" resources instead. At this point we are waiting\n// for the server to tell us that this resource should be either moved to the \"wildcard\" resources,\n// or dropped. Resources in \"wildcard\" category are only added there or dropped from there by the\n// server. Resources from both \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories can become \"requested\"\n// \"complete\" resources if we subscribe to them again.\n//\n// The delta subscription state transitions between the two scenarios depending on whether we are\n// subscribed to wildcard resource or not. Nothing special happens when we transition from \"no\n// wildcard subscription\" to \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, but when transitioning in the other\n// direction, we drop all the resources in \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories.\nclass DeltaSubscriptionState : public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\npublic:\n  DeltaSubscriptionState(std::string type_url, UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks& watch_map,","numLines":80,"startLine":1,"totalLines":183}}}
